British Military Circles Attach Great Importance to Soviet-Turkish Negotiations; Believe it is Related to the Situation in the Black Sea; Lithuania Discusses Soviet Proposals 17

London: Military and political figures here have focused their attention on the Soviet-Turkish negotiations. It is believed that the Soviet Union is eager to protect itself from the possibility of British naval and air forces attacking and destroying the Baku oil fields via the Black Sea. Therefore, it is now putting pressure on Turkey to lock the Black Sea, but it is believed that Turkey will not disappoint the Allied countries. (Reuters, 5th)

Geneva: News has been received here from Paris that French political figures are paying close attention to the Soviet-Turkish negotiations. French political circles believe that these negotiations involve the issue of Turkey recognizing the accomplished facts within Poland. If Turkey follows the Soviet Union's opinion, other countries in the Balkan Entente may also follow suit. (Haitong, 5th)

Moscow: Political figures in Moscow say that the Turkish representative has received instructions from his government to continue negotiations, so the Soviet-Turkish negotiations that were suspended on October 2 can be reopened. Diplomatic circles here are rife with rumors that the Soviet government has proposed the following key points to the Turkish Foreign Minister: (1) Warships of belligerent countries are not allowed to pass through the Dardanelles Strait during wartime; (2) Conclude a Soviet-Turkish mutual assistance treaty; (3) In fact, the Soviet Union will undermine Turkey's relationship with the British-French alliance. (Haitong, 5th)

Turkish Capital: According to a semi-official statement here today, the negotiations between the Soviet Union and Turkey are proceeding in a friendly atmosphere and will continue for several days. (Reuters, 4th)

Turkish Capital: According to political figures here, the negotiations between Russia and Turkey currently underway in Moscow are expected to be successfully concluded this Saturday. At that time, Foreign Minister Saracoglu will visit Romanian Foreign Minister Gafencu in Constanta on his way back to the country for talks. (Haitong, 5th)

Moscow: Turkish Foreign Minister Saracoglu, accompanied by the Turkish Ambassador to the Soviet Union, Yaktai, visited Soviet Defense Commissar Voroshilov yesterday and held a lengthy conversation. Saracoglu then visited Soviet People's Commissar for Foreign Trade Mikoyan. Soviet Ambassador to Turkey Terentiev also participated. (Haitong, 5th)

Istanbul: Turkish Foreign Minister Saracoglu's talks in Moscow have been delayed. Although official circles have not criticized it, the public has become greatly uneasy. Newspapers authorized by the government vaguely state that even the slightest sacrifice that harms Turkey's sovereignty and honor cannot be recognized. This is Turkey's task. According to reliable sources, but not confirmed by official circles, the Soviet Union has requested to sign mutual assistance treaties with the Balkan and Black Sea countries, which are the same as those being negotiated by the Soviet Union with the Baltic countries. Another message said that the Soviet Union had informed Saracoglu that the Soviet Union must establish naval bases in Romania's Constanta port and maintain the right to transport troops through the Balkan Peninsula countries. It is heard that among the important events discussed by Saracoglu in the Soviet capital, in addition to the events that are directly related to Soviet-Turkish relations, there are also those that affect the Balkan Consultative Countries, allowing them to be the issue of Romania. Although the true nature of these discussions is still very vague, Turkish newspapers are fiercely criticizing the rumors that the Balkan Peninsula countries are abandoning their neutral status and tending towards democratic countries. Diplomatic circles hinted that Moscow is putting pressure on Saracoglu, but said that no matter what happens, Turkey's position and its promises to Britain and France will not be affected. (Reuters, 5th)

London: General Ape, the leader of the Turkish military delegation, visited General Ironside, Commander-in-Chief of the British Army, at the British War Office today. (Reuters, 4th)

Lithuanian Capital: The cabinet met today to discuss the Soviet proposal, the content of which is said to be military in nature. It was previously reported that Foreign Minister Urbsys, who was going to Moscow again today, may postpone his departure until tomorrow. (Reuters, 5th)

Lithuanian Capital: Lithuanian Foreign Minister Urbsys has returned to the country from Moscow by special plane to report to the cabinet on the course of the talks. It is heard that the Soviet government has put forward several proposals, which the cabinet discussed until late at night before dispersing, but its content is currently kept secret. (Reuters, 5th)

Moscow: Well-informed sources here indicate that Latvia has agreed to the following requests made by the Soviet Union: (1) The Latvian ports of Liepāja and Ventspils must be fortified, and the Soviet Union may station approximately 30,000 troops in the above two ports; (2) Grant the Soviet Union greater power in Latvia's trade policy. Last night, Latvian Foreign Minister Munters and Latvian legal advisor Chevlinis began drafting an agreement with representatives of the Soviet government. (Haitong, 5th)

Swiss Capital: According to news from the Finnish capital, the claim that the Soviet government invited Finnish Foreign Minister Erkko to go to Moscow is not accurate, but it has been confirmed that the Soviet Union has again requested that the Finnish government not fortify the Aland Islands. (Havas, 5th)

Moscow: Estonian Foreign Minister Selter and Soviet representative Palchirov exchanged the ratified text of the Soviet-Estonian Mutual Assistance Treaty in the Estonian capital last night. This treaty took effect after ratification. The content stipulates that the Soviet Union has the right to establish naval bases and airfields on the two Estonian islands of Oosil and Dagö, placing the Gulf of Riga under its control. (Reuters, 5th)

Britain Recognizes New Polish President 18

London: According to the Ministry of Information, after all former ministers of the Polish government recognized the new president, the Polish ambassador to Britain notified the British government that Mościcki had resigned and was succeeded by Raczkiewicz. After receiving this notification, the British government has now recognized Raczkiewicz as President of the Polish Republic. It is reported that Mościcki is currently residing in the Romanian capital and is preparing to reside in Switzerland. The Swiss Federal Council has already approved. (Reuters, 5th)

New York Foreign Exchange Market 19

New York: The pound price in the New York foreign exchange market rose slightly today due to strong commercial demand and rumors of an imminent European truce. The opening pound price was 4.03, and the closing price was 4.05 and 5/8. The closing price yesterday was 4.03 and 1/8. The forward pound price also improved, which reflects optimism in people's minds. (Reuters, 4th)

German Invasion of Poland Leaves 50,000-60,000 Casualties 20

Belgian Capital: The semi-official Belgian news agency recently issued a Berlin report stating that, according to reports, the total number of officer and soldier deaths and injuries resulting from yesterday's battles within Poland was 50,000 to 60,000. (Havas, 4th)

Germany Plans to Monopolize Trade with Neutral Countries to Strengthen Economic Warfare Capabilities 21

Danish Capital Dispatch: The political reporter stationed in Berlin claims that according to informed sources in Berlin, the German government will soon invite neutral countries to participate in a trade conference in order to change the entire current trade system in Europe. It is heard that former President of the German National Bank, Schacht, has drafted a plan asking neutral countries to transport all their exports to Germany, which will then resell them to other neutral countries. (Reuters, 5th)

Danish Capital: Negotiations on German-Danish commercial relations began today at the Danish Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The main topic of discussion was the various problems that have arisen in German-Danish commercial relations after Britain implemented a blockade policy. (Haitong, 5th)

Latvian Capital: The Latvian commercial delegation will travel to Berlin next week at the invitation of Germany to negotiate the promotion of trade between the two countries. (Reuters, 5th)

Yugoslav Capital: The German economic delegation has been here for some time negotiating a commercial agreement with the Yugoslav government. The German side intends to order various raw materials and requests immediate delivery, but is unwilling to pay for the goods in cash, only promising to exchange them for military equipment and various machines "as soon as possible." This has not been accepted by the Yugoslav government, and current negotiations have encountered difficulties. The plenary meeting originally scheduled for the two delegations to be held within days has been postponed indefinitely. In addition, it is heard that the British Commercial Counselor has met with the Yugoslav Minister of Commerce, Drais, to inform him that his country is willing to purchase grain and raw materials from Yugoslavia. For this reason, the Yugoslav government's attitude towards Germany has become tougher. Germany fears that after the negotiations break down, Yugoslavia will contact Britain, and also because the Soviet Union may provide various raw materials under more favorable conditions, it is not eager to conclude an agreement with Yugoslavia. (Havas, 5th)

Paris: Well-informed sources here recently said that since the Soviet Union is putting pressure on the Baltic coastal countries and Germany is putting pressure on the Scandinavian Peninsula countries, there is a possibility that these countries may be forced to become war zones in a short period of time. As far as the Soviet Union is concerned, according to information obtained from Rome, the Soviet government has concentrated 600 aircraft and 20 army divisions in the Kunlun area on the border with Latvia. In addition, in accordance with the mutual assistance treaty it signed with Estonia, the Soviet government originally intended to send troops to strategic locations in that country, but it sent troops before that country ratified the treaty. On the other hand, the Soviet Union also made demands on Finland for certain privileges for certain ports in that country. Judging from this, the Soviet Union intends to maintain strategic bases on the Baltic coast, and the more the better. As far as Germany is concerned, it is heard that the German government has sent a strongly worded note to the Norwegian government, demanding that it supply the country with certain goods, otherwise it will send aircraft to bomb it. The threatening methods it has taken against neutral countries can be seen from this. Regarding this, people in Sweden expect that Germany and the Soviet Union will soon force the Scandinavian Peninsula countries to stop trading with Britain and France and instead sell various goods to Germany and the Soviet Union. (Germany needs a part of the pig iron supplied from the Scandinavian Peninsula countries). These countries are extremely uneasy about this. However, responsible officials in Paris still said that Germany and the Soviet Union's strategies are bound to fail. (Havas, 5th)

German Submarine Sinks Greek Ship; French Submarine Captures German Ship; Estonian Ship Detained by Germans 22

London. The Greek steamship "Taimantis" was sunk today by a German submarine in British waters, 60 miles from the coast. All crew members have been rescued. (4th, Havas dispatch)

London. Twenty-eight crew members of the Greek steamship "Taimantis," which was sunk by a German submarine, who escaped danger were landed last night by the submarine at Ventley Bay in Kent County. It is reported that five members of the local militia witnessed the submarine submerging into the sea, but were unable to detain it. The rescued individuals were confined to the submarine for 36 hours. It is said that the Germans treated them well. Six of them require hospital treatment, but their conditions are not severe. (4th, Reuters dispatch)

London. Responsible sources here claim that in the past week, only 836 tons of British ships have been sunk by the Germans. The German claim that a British merchant ship rammed a German submarine is entirely unfounded. They also deny that the British authorities have used submarines in the current conflict. (5th, Reuters dispatch)

London. A German ship of 8,000 tons, which was loading iron ore in Luleå, Sweden, recently entered a minefield near the island of Borkum in the East Frisian Islands of German territory in the North Sea. It is reported that it struck a mine and sank. The fate of the crew is unknown. However, the Germans have now seized the Estonian ship "Järni" to compensate for this loss. According to a Gothenburg, Sweden, newspaper, the "Järni" was carrying lumber to Antwerp, Belgium, when it was seized near Visby by a German destroyer and taken to a German port. Furthermore, according to a dispatch from Danzig, a large coal ship flying the Finnish flag was seen aground on the outer beach of Jäschke Island yesterday, refusing assistance, giving the impression that it was a German ship and that there may be detained crew members on board. (5th, Reuters)

Paris. It has been learned that the French submarine that captured a German cargo ship yesterday and brought it back to a French port traveled over a thousand miles, which is a remarkable achievement for a submarine. (5th, Reuters dispatch)

Copenhagen, Denmark. Cannon fire was heard yesterday off the western coast of Denmark. It is generally believed that this was due to a naval battle near the German island of Heligoland. (5th, Havas News Agency dispatch)

Stockholm, Sweden. After repeated violations of territorial waters by German submarines, the Swedish government has decided to form a fleet to patrol the coast. This fleet includes one battleship, two destroyers, two submarines, and several smaller warships. The naval authorities have also borrowed one hundred merchant ships from various shipping companies, equipped them with weapons, and ordered them to assist in searching within territorial waters. (5th, Havas dispatch)

Copenhagen, Denmark. The "National Daily" here recently published a dispatch from its Berlin correspondent stating that several Danish ships detained by the Germans will be released after confiscating the cargo they carry. German officials also confirmed that if the British contraband list is not revised, Germany will launch an "economic war" with all its strength, regardless of the impact on neutral countries. (5th, Havas dispatch)

Berlin. Political figures here, commenting on Germany's intensification of economic warfare against Britain, stated that Germany's adoption of this measure was not proactive, but was forced as a response. Germany is willing to engage in fair warfare. Germany's chivalrous conduct in the first month after the outbreak of the war can prove this, and the statements of neutral observers can also be cited as sufficient evidence. The new action by the British Admiralty to arm merchant ships is an extreme violation of the laws of maritime warfare in international law. Merely arming merchant ships cannot be regarded as converting them into warships, but the direct order from the British Admiralty to attack German warships has blurred the distinction between combatant and non-combatant. Therefore, Germany has a need to intensify economic warfare. (5th, Haitong dispatch)

London. The Information Department recently issued a communiqué stating that in the week from the 23rd to the 30th of last month, a total of 33,000 tons of various contraband goods destined for Germany were intercepted by British warships. In total, the number of contraband goods intercepted in the four weeks since the start of the war has reached 289,000 tons. (4th, Havas dispatch)

Daladier Signs Agreement with Czech Envoy; Stipulates Formation of Czech Army in France 23

Paris. Prime Minister Daladier signed an agreement yesterday with Osuský, the Czechoslovakian envoy to France, stipulating the formation of a Czech army in France to fight against Germany and seek the restoration of lost Czech territory. (4th, Havas dispatch)

Western Front; Intermittent Artillery Battles Between Two Armies; Germans Evacuate Civilians from Various Border Towns; French Aircraft Reconnaissance Work Very Successful 24

Paris. The General Headquarters issued communiqué No. 61, stating, "Our advanced units are constantly patrolling in various locations on the front lines. The enemy once attempted to advance south of Bemasans City but was repelled by our army. In addition, one of our submarines intercepted an enemy merchant ship somewhere at sea and ordered it to sail to one of our ports." (4th, Havas dispatch)

Paris. The General Headquarters issued communiqué No. 62, stating, "Artillery battles occurred intermittently in several places on the front lines last night." (5th, Havas dispatch)

Paris. The General Headquarters issued a communiqué regarding the results of air combat over the past month, stating that in September, a total of eight of our pursuit aircraft were shot down, and a total of thirty German pursuit aircraft were shot down. In addition, our aircraft have repeatedly conducted reconnaissance work and have been very successful, taking thousands of photographs. The enemy's anti-aircraft batteries and air force were unable to prevent this. As a result, the construction situation of the Siegfried Line is fully known to our military staff. As for German aircraft, they have not yet conducted reconnaissance flights within our country. (4th, Havas dispatch)

London. Military critics here are gradually adopting the view that the German army will take the road through the Netherlands to attack. The news that the German army is actively reinforcing the Siegfried Line opposite Belgium shows that they want to protect their left flank in this attack. Moreover, this is the only place where they can use the mechanized units and rapid attack tactics that have been very effective in Poland with the hope of success. According to an announcement by the Information Department today, the German Minister of Aviation, Göring, the Minister of Propaganda, Goebbels, and other leaders of the National Socialist Party purchased a large amount of butter from Britain several months before the outbreak of the war. It is said that it was sent every week by an employee of a large wool export company from Bradford to the aforementioned leaders. (5th, Reuters dispatch)

Paris. The first group of French war correspondents is scheduled to go to the front lines tomorrow to report on the war. These people are all famous writers. Kessel, the founder of "Paris-Soir," and Tauzilles, a reporter for "Gringoire," are among them. As for foreign journalists, except for a few reporters from British and American newspapers, they are not allowed to enter or leave the war zone. (5th, Havas dispatch)

French Parliament Declares Recess; To Prevent Communist Activities; Many Communist Deputies to be Arrested 25

Paris. Since the government announced the temporary recess of the Parliament, people in the lounges of the Senate and the House of Representatives have unanimously praised it, and said that many Communist deputies will soon be arrested, and their arrest warrants have already been issued. (5th, Havas)

Paris. After the cabinet held a State Council meeting yesterday morning, the government gazette published an order today stipulating that the Parliament should be adjourned immediately. Political figures commented on this, saying that this move is extremely important. Although the government dissolved the Communist Party on the 26th of last month, the privileges enjoyed by the party's members of Parliament are still valid. According to the Constitution, this privilege is limited to the parliamentary session. Once the session ends, it will immediately lose its effect. Now that the Parliament has been adjourned, the privileges enjoyed by the deputies will be automatically canceled, and the government can punish them in accordance with ordinary laws when necessary. The authorities have also, at the request of the military authorities, begun investigating the activities of the party's deputies. If the deputies are found to have formed a new party under a false name, they will be brought to justice. However, the temporary adjournment of Parliament does not stop its activities, and the government can still convene it at any time, which should be in the second half of November. The full powers enjoyed by the government will then expire, and the Parliament will have to be asked to re-pass the Full Powers Act. (5th, Havas dispatch)

Paris. The municipal halls of various towns in the Seine Province, which are presided over by members of the Communist Party, have been ordered to be dissolved by the Ministry of the Interior, and new municipal halls have been appointed to exercise their functions on their behalf. (5th, Havas dispatch)

Canberra. The regulations preventing the export of capital from Australia were promulgated in the gazette today. The methods are the same as those published by Britain and Canada. (5th, Reuters dispatch)

British Dominions Send Representatives to London

The Hague. US Bomber Squadron Patrols Over Fiji; Submarine Squadron to Arrive in Manila Within Month; Chongqing Newspaper Praises US Navy as Stabilizing Force in the Far East 29

Manila. Fourteen bombers that arrived here earlier from Hawaii, from today, five of them have started flying to familiarize themselves with the terrain, while patrolling the skies over the Philippines. These aircraft are currently based at Cañacao Bay across from Manila Bay. The aircraft carrier "Langley" is also anchored there. In addition, six US submarines sent here for reassignment are expected to arrive here within this month. (5th, Associated Press dispatch)

Washington. Reliable sources claim that twelve US Navy bombers patrol the Caribbean Sea from the United States to northern South America "from dawn to dusk" every day. US Navy officials neither confirmed nor denied this. It is widely believed that this patrol is the first step in establishing a "security belt" around Panama. (5th, Associated Press dispatch)

Chongqing. Chinese sources here believe that the US Navy's strong presence in the Pacific is a stabilizing force in the Far East situation. Although Japan's continental expansion policy has not achieved much to date, if there were no US power to control it in the Pacific, Japan might expand southward and shake the position of Hong Kong, Singapore, the Philippines, and the Dutch East Indies. In the previous Great War, the United States focused on Europe. In the current Great War, the United States is focusing on Japanese aggression. In short, as long as the US Far East policy does not change, Japan will never be able to realize its ambitions. (5th, Associated Press dispatch)

President of Japanese Seiyukai Party Nakajima Attacked; Bullets Miss; Assailant Escapes 30

Tokyo. Nakajima Chikuhei, the president of the reform faction of the Seiyukai Party, was shot at by someone with a gun near his home at around 8 p.m. on the 4th when he was returning home in a car. US Senate Continues Debate on Neutrality Act Amendment; Senator Johnson Suggests Mediating the War 31

Washington. The Senate continued to debate the Neutrality Act amendment today. Senator Connally, a Democrat, gave a speech in support of the amendment proposed by the government, saying that if the arms embargo is not lifted, Germany could easily use it as an excuse to sink American merchant ships. He also said that US defense, both naval, land and air, must be strengthened. In addition, Republican Senator Vandenberg, a key isolationist, insisted on maintaining the arms embargo. (4th, Havas dispatch)

Washington. Senator Tom Connally, yesterday moved in the Senate, advocating that the government's Neutrality Act amendment be sent back to the Foreign Relations Committee for reconsideration, so that the committee divides the "cash and carry" clause into two parts, and then returns it to the Senate for discussion. (5th, Associated Press dispatch)

Washington. Senator Johnson, a Democrat from Colorado, proposed yesterday in the Senate, asking President Roosevelt to cooperate with the leaders of various neutral countries to bring about an "immediate ceasefire" in Europe. Johnson said this is the best time to mediate in the current situation, and other neutral countries are waiting for the United States to initiate it first. This proposal has been submitted to the Senate Foreign Relations Committee for review. (5th, Associated Press dispatch)

Washington. Republican Senator Johnson submitted a draft resolution to the Senate, requesting President Roosevelt to join with various neutral countries to mediate and urge the European belligerent countries to stop the war immediately. Diplomatic figures here commented on this, saying that only the President and the Senate Foreign Relations Committee have the right to initiate this matter. Johnson's actions are a kind of strategy, even if it leads to victory achieved by violence being recognized. (4th, Havas dispatch)

Washington. While the Senate continued to debate the government's Neutrality Act today, Republican Senator Johnson introduced a resolution asking President Roosevelt to join other neutral countries in urging an immediate ceasefire in Europe. Democrat Connally, who had previously opposed the government on various domestic issues, now supports the government's new Neutrality Act, saying that if the arms embargo and restrictions on American shipping are not lifted, Germany will soon sink American merchant ships. Republican Vandenberg opposed lifting the arms embargo, saying that this action is a non-neutral act, and if this habit is cultivated, other non-neutral acts will easily follow, such as the United States scheming many things outside the war to assist those it favors, and ultimately being drawn into the war. (4th, Reuters dispatch)

Washington. Secretary of State Hull issued a formal statement today, saying that the US government does not recognize unlimited interference with the legality of American merchant ships. At the same time, Hull warned American merchant ships of the special dangers of sailing into the vicinity of belligerent waters. (4th, Reuters dispatch)

Japanese Cabinet Establishes Ministry of Trade; Storm in Ministry of Foreign Affairs; Director of Commercial Affairs Bureau Matsushima Resigns; Foreign Minister Nomura Criticized by Subordinates 32

Tokyo. After the Cabinet decided to establish a Ministry of Trade to absorb the Commercial Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, a bizarre situation has occurred in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Matsushima, the Director of the Commercial Affairs Bureau, angrily resigned yesterday morning, saying that if the ship does not listen to the captain, then the captain can only leave the ship. As a result, the six section chiefs and several junior officials of the Commercial Affairs Bureau also resigned one after another. Then, 150 senior officials of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs held a meeting to discuss this situation for a long time, and finally decided to ask Foreign Minister Nomura to attend the meeting at 5:15 p.m. yesterday to question him, criticizing him for betraying his faith in supporting the establishment of the Ministry of Trade and demanding his resignation. However, Nomura's attitude was firm and he did not accept the request, saying that implementing national policy is to prioritize the unity of the cabinet. The staff of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs then requested that important political and economic diplomacy should be unified under the control of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and passed a resolution stating that all directors and secretaries of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs are united and firmly opposed to the main points of the establishment of the Ministry of Trade. The government now believes that this turmoil is an internal matter of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The staff of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs again convened a meeting today to consider protesting to Prime Minister Abe. (5th, Reuters News Agency dispatch)

Tokyo. All section chiefs and administrative officials of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs held a meeting in the conference room at 8 p.m. on the 4th, advocating opposition to the establishment of the Ministry of Trade. It was resolved that each department and bureau should elect one section chief representative and one administrative official representative to form an executive committee to carry out the opposition movement, and the meeting would not disperse until the goal was achieved. After the meeting, the following declaration was issued: The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is not opposed to the establishment of the Ministry of Trade. For the sake of completing the current general mobilization system, it originally advocated the establishment of a strong industrial trade ministry or economic ministry that included the production and distribution sectors. However, now that diplomacy is not unified - political diplomacy and economic diplomacy - but implements a unified diplomacy, it is absolutely impossible to deal with the difficult international situation. Therefore, we firmly oppose the Ministry of Trade directly participating in diplomatic work, and firmly believe that the organic union of political diplomacy and economic diplomacy can realize the development of overseas trade. Thus, an attempt was made to establish a powerful industrial trade ministry to strengthen a unified diplomacy externally, and to unify trade, production, distribution and other sectors internally to promote Japan's economic development. However, the main points of the establishment of the Ministry of Trade decided by the Cabinet this time not only failed to thoroughly include the production and distribution sectors, but also recognized that the Ministry of Trade could directly issue orders and direct affairs to overseas commercial officials and consuls general. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has always advocated the unification of diplomacy, so all section chiefs and administrative officials must unanimously oppose the main points of the establishment of the Ministry of Trade decided this time. (5th, Domei dispatch)

Tokyo. The preparatory committee for the Ministry of Trade decided by the cabinet meeting on the 3rd held its first meeting at the Prime Minister's official residence at 2 p.m. on the 5th. Chairman Karasawa and the various committee members attended. First, they discussed and reviewed the order and other administrative matters, and then proceeded with substantive deliberations. In addition, the new Ministry of Trade decided to transfer some of the affairs of the Commerce and Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Matsushima, the Director of the Commerce Bureau, submitted his resignation based on his position. Also, other foreign affairs officials opposed the new Ministry of Trade's organization. However, the government seems determined to implement it according to the established policy. Prime Minister Abe and Foreign Minister Nomura will also express their determination at the regular Councilors' meeting on the 5th, hoping to realize it in accordance with the cabinet decision. (5th, Domei dispatch)

Berlin, Rome Report; Japan Withdraws from Anti-Comintern Pact; Tokyo Believes It Is a Misunderstanding 33

Tokyo. The reports from Berlin and Rome that Japanese Foreign Minister Nomura has announced his withdrawal from the Anti-Comintern Pact are unfounded. It is believed here that Germany and Italy are obviously spreading rumors based on Nomura's speech at the National Local Governors' Conference on October 2. Japanese sources claim that the Foreign Minister did not mention the Anti-Comintern Pact in his speech that day, but only said that negotiations to strengthen the tripartite Anti-Comintern Pact would be suspended due to the development of the European situation. (5th, Reuters dispatch)

Xinhua Daily News Comments; British Warships Withdraw 34

Chongqing. The CCP organ Xinhua Daily News commented today on the British naval authorities' withdrawal of five out of ten British gunboats from the Yangtze River between Shanghai and Hankou, saying that this decision may have a major significance for the future development of the Far East. Therefore, the Chinese must carefully consider this matter. Given the outbreak of the European War, the withdrawal of British gunboats is naturally expected. What the Chinese should pay attention to is not the withdrawal of the gunboats themselves, but the gradual withdrawal of British power from the Far East and the subsequent changes in British Far East policy. Britain has huge interests in the Far East, but since the outbreak of the European War, these interests have been under very strong pressure, and therefore it has compromised with Japan in the hope of protecting its interests. However, history has proven the repeated errors of British Far East policy. The Anglo-Japanese Treaty of 1894 helped Japan defeat China, and as a result, Japan, a second-rate country, became a first-rate country in the Far East. The Anglo-Japanese Alliance of 1902 resulted in Japan defeating old Russia. Although the Anglo-Japanese Alliance was abolished due to American opposition, its spirit has occupied an important part in British Far East policy from the Mukden Incident in 1931 to the present. Japan is determined to eliminate the interests of third countries in China. Britain is well aware of this, but since the Mukden Incident, Britain has consistently adopted a policy of compromise with Japan. It can now be frankly said that if one believes that Britain is helping China to resist Japanese aggression, it is more accurate to say that Britain hopes that Japanese aggression in China will end within a certain limit. For many years, the British government's efforts have been largely devoted to this goal. China is indeed unfortunate, but Britain is also unfortunate, and its rights and prestige have become sacrifices of this policy. British rulers do not want a strong and independent China. The talk about reopening Anglo-Japanese talks clearly indicates the path that events will follow. We now want to warn Britain that Japan's policy of expelling third countries' rights in China will never change. No matter what kind of compromise Britain makes, it will not affect China's determination to continue resisting Japan. Furthermore, Britain and Japan cannot solve the problem of the Far East alone. At the same time, we hope that the British people will prevent their government from casting the same mistakes it made in Europe, and we hope that the Chinese people will pay attention to the international conspiracy currently underway in the Far East. (5th, Reuters News Agency dispatch)

Freight Transportation Between Hanoi and Kunming Halted 35

Kunming. Passenger train services between Kunming and Hanoi, which had just resumed on Sunday after being interrupted by landslides caused by heavy floods, were disrupted again today due to three landslides between Kunming and Jiangyuan (transliteration). The situation in the flooded areas of Kunming has greatly improved. After three days of dry weather, the surrounding roads are no longer flooded. Farmers are now busy clearing the rotten vegetables in the fields. (5th, Reuters News Agency dispatch)

US Gunboat Docked in Chongqing Damaged in Collision 36

Chongqing. The US gunboat "Tutuila," docked in Chongqing, was struck by a ferryboat in heavy fog yesterday. It is expected to be repaired in the city within a few weeks. The ferryboat was swept away by the rapids of the Yangtze River and collided with the "Tutuila," creating a hole four feet wide and nearly ten feet high in the hull. There were no casualties. However, two people on the ferryboat were knocked overboard and were quickly rescued by nearby sailboats. Sailors on the gunboat immediately began pumping water. Fortunately, an engineer who previously worked at the Shanghai company that built the ship is now in Chongqing. After inspecting the damage, he expressed the opinion that the ship could be repaired in the city without much difficulty. (5th, Reuters dispatch)

News from Northern Jiangsu: Fierce Fighting in Guanyun's Yangji for Five Days and Nights; Chinese Troops in Xuzhou Approaching the Suburbs; Japanese Invasion of Huai'an Foiled; Puppet Troops in Yangzhou Under Japanese Surveillance 37

Taixian Correspondence: In recent days, there have been repeated clashes between Chinese and Japanese troops in various counties in northern Jiangsu. A summary follows:

Guanyun: On the night of September 18th, the Guanyun Regular Brigade fiercely attacked the Japanese troops in Yangji. The next day, when they attacked the fort, platoon leader Zhang Tongfeng and more than 20 soldiers heroically sacrificed themselves in a mine explosion. Nine Japanese soldiers were killed or captured alive. The remaining Japanese troops continued to resist from a blockhouse. After five days and nights of stalemate, the entire town of Yangji was reduced to scorched earth. On the 22nd, three Japanese planes escorted approximately 200 Japanese soldiers to reinforce Xiangshuikou, Xinpu, Banpu, and Dayishan. Except for the Japanese troops at Dayishan, who were blocked by Chinese troops, the rest had entered Yangji fort and attempted to cut off the Chinese troops' retreat. On the 23rd and 24th, Japanese planes bombed the Chinese troops in shifts, forcing the Chinese troops to retreat to their original positions.

Haizhou: Japanese planes have been unusually active in Haizhou recently. On the 21st, they dropped three or four bombs at Zhangjiadian and Longrong. On the 22nd, they dropped three or four bombs at Xiaoyao. They dropped more than 20 bombs near Tongxingji Longwokou, and more than 10 bombs in Xin'an Town. On the 24th, they dropped more than 10 bombs near Yangji and five or six bombs near Tanggou Tangjian. Despite the activity of Japanese planes, the morale of the Chinese soldiers and civilians remains extremely high.

Ganyu: After the Ganyu Chinese Army Regular Brigade occupied Ganyu County, they captured a significant amount of Japanese light and heavy weaponry. When they subsequently attacked Huandunbu, the Japanese troops suffered heavy losses. However, they failed to firmly occupy Shahe Town due to the arrival of Japanese reinforcements.

Xuzhou: In the Xuzhou area, there have been frequent clashes between Chinese and Japanese troops recently. Fierce fighting occurred on the 17th and 20th, with four Japanese soldiers killed and more wounded. Therefore, Japanese troops are heavily stationed inside and outside the city and around the railway station to prevent Chinese troops from launching a surprise attack. However, the Chinese troops are distributed in various villages, waiting for an opportunity to attack. Furthermore, a unit of the Chinese Army's general brigade arrived near Xuzhou to monitor the movements of the Japanese troops and launch a counter-offensive.

Huai'an: The Japanese troops in Huai'an have been scheming to invade the south, but have not succeeded. At approximately 8:00 AM on September 24th, a combined Japanese infantry, cavalry, and artillery force of more than 200 men advanced towards Huafangtou, Handong, and Shazhuang. They first bombarded the area with heavy artillery, followed by machine-gun fire. The Chinese troops also bravely resisted. However, the Japanese troops resorted to inhumane tactics, releasing tear gas. To avoid the gas, the Chinese troops quickly retreated. As a result, the two locations were occupied by the Japanese troops. At 8:00 PM, Chinese reinforcements arrived and launched a large-scale counter-offensive while the Japanese troops were still consolidating their positions. The Chinese troops, with high morale, attacked from multiple directions. The Japanese troops, caught off guard, retreated into the city. Huafangtou and Shazhuang were recaptured by the Chinese troops. On the same day, the Japanese troops in Huai'an dispatched another unit of approximately 100 Japanese and puppet troops, with two small artillery pieces and four light and heavy machine guns, to Huangtu Bridge outside the east gate. After fierce resistance from the local self-defense forces, the Japanese troops used their superior firepower to launch a fierce attack and forcibly occupied the area, destroying more than a dozen civilian houses in retaliation. However, they were ambushed by Chinese troops and retreated back into the city.

Funing: On September 19th, Japanese troops in Funing dispatched more than 40 Japanese and puppet troops, with many light and heavy machine guns, to attack the Chinese troops' position at Xiaozhaoguan. They came into contact with the headquarters of the Chinese Regular Brigade stationed there. The Chinese troops resisted using fortified defenses, preventing the Japanese troops from succeeding, and forcing them to retreat back into the city. In this battle, one Japanese officer was killed. It is also reported that the Japanese troops in Funing are currently building 30 two-section boats, each section capable of being carried by two people. Their intentions are unclear.

Yangzhou: The Japanese troops in Xishan, having been ambushed by Chinese guerrilla units, are feeling uneasy. On the 22nd, 50 to 60 Japanese troops from Yangzhou reinforced Xishan, but the next morning, they returned to Yangzhou in the same two trucks. In addition, approximately 200 Japanese and puppet troops are stationed at Xiannvmiao. Puppet troops are stationed as sentries, seven or eight at each location, at Touerdiao Bridge and Sanyuan Bridge Jiangjia Bridge. Japanese troops also send out sentries to monitor the puppet troops. Furthermore, a Japanese shallow-water warship is patrolling the Xian Shao River to protect bridges and waterways and prevent sabotage by Chinese troops.

Jianghua Troops Requested to Launch Night Attack; Japanese and Puppets Defending County Seat 38

Jingjiang Correspondence: Jingjiang is a small county in northern Jiangsu. Since being occupied by the Japanese and puppets, the city, which is only three miles in circumference, and the eighteen miles from the city to the Jiangbian of Bawai Port have been placed under their control. The other townships attached to the city are still under Chinese control. A small unit of Chinese troops attacked a puppet police station outside the west gate late at night. In the darkness, the two sides exchanged fire, resulting in casualties on both sides. Puppet Inspector Ni was also injured. Chinese mobile units often use various opportunities in the countryside to ambush Japanese and puppet troops, making it difficult for the Japanese and puppet troops to track them down. Therefore, they are only able to defend the small city and are unable to do anything else. Recently, a traitor named Cai Dekui was captured in Baiyi Town. He was shot for being a Japanese electrician. The Japanese and puppet troops, fearing the Chinese troops, have issued county resident certificates to all residents in the city and have organized them into baojia (a system of household registration and control). New residents whose names are not on the register are not allowed to receive certificates and are accused of being anti-Japanese elements. Therefore, the population of the city has not increased. Most residents live in the Huangju and Wumawei areas.

Yangshuyuan, Wuxi, Harassed by Japanese Troops; Qian Junshi Dies for His Country 39

Wuxi Correspondence: Yangshuyuan, Wuxi, is near Taihu Lake. When the Chinese troops retreated westward the year before last, many people sought refuge there, regarding it as an isolated paradise. This spring, Qian Junshi, the district chief of the Tenth District, cooperated with the guerrillas to maintain order. Last month, it was suddenly reported that the Japanese military police from the urban area had sent more than 20 Japanese soldiers to the town to keep an eye on the guerrillas. To avoid sacrificing the town, the guerrillas did not take action. The Japanese troops soon retreated. On the afternoon of September 30th, more than 20 Japanese soldiers arrived in a boat at Caishentang, four or five miles from the town. Suddenly, there was intense gunfire from both sides of the river. The boatman was shot dead, and the boat capsized. At that time, more than 20 Japanese soldiers were killed, two were captured, and one escaped in the chaos and returned to the city to report. On the night of the 30th, a large force of Japanese and puppet troops arrived and surrounded Yangshuyuan, demanding the surrender of the perpetrators and the bodies of the Japanese soldiers. Qian Junshi led his troops to resist. The Japanese troops set fire to the town. Qian Junshi bravely took the lead and died after being shot several times. Later, Chinese reinforcements arrived and drove back the Japanese and puppet troops. However, before retreating, the Japanese and puppet troops took several townspeople with them. The town was burned down, and the town hall and the new altar were destroyed. The losses were immeasurable. Later, Chinese guerrillas extinguished the fire and collected Qian Junshi's body. The townspeople expressed their respect for Qian Junshi, who died with great spirit. However, all the residents of the town evacuated after hearing the alarm.

Fujian Province Expands Winter Cultivation Campaign; Implements Grain Management Measures in Various Counties 40

Fuzhou Correspondence: Since the outbreak of the war of resistance, Fujian Province has promoted winter cultivation to increase agricultural production and achieve self-sufficiency in food during wartime. However, the winter cultivation campaign in the sixth year was rushed due to time constraints, and publicity and guidance were not widespread. Therefore, the planting area of winter crops was only more than 2 million mu. By the seventh year, the winter cultivation area had increased to more than 3.2 million mu. This year's winter cultivation period is approaching again. The provincial government has decided to further expand the campaign. The Provincial Agricultural Improvement Bureau has drafted a plan, divided into two steps: publicity and implementation. In terms of publicity, in addition to using various oral and written methods and various occasions, they will also use the universal National Monthly Meeting and wartime civil schools to lecture on winter cultivation issues to achieve greater results. In terms of implementation, in addition to mobilizing all farmers in the province to work hard in winter cultivation, they will also promote the participation of rural women, who account for half of the population. For winter cultivation loans, the Cooperation Affairs Administration under the Construction Department will coordinate the handling and has obtained the consent of the Provincial Bank to increase the loan amount. According to the wartime situation, the counties in the province are divided into three types: A, B, and C. Type A includes 16 coastal counties such as Wenhou, Type B includes 9 counties such as Shouning, and Type C includes 13 counties such as Nanping. This classification method is designed to concentrate grain production in the rear to avoid losses during the outbreak of war. The loan recipients are loyal farmers with farming ability, heads of households, with fixed addresses and cultivated land, whether they are members of the cooperative or not, can apply for loans. Cooperative members' loans are handled according to the credit loan method. Non-member loans should gather five to thirty people to form a cooperative winter cultivation group, which is introduced by the cooperative or guaranteed by a reliable guarantor. The interest rate on these loans is very low, and the repayment period is limited to six months. The amount that each person can borrow is three yuan in Type A counties, five yuan in Type B counties, and ten yuan in Type C counties. The selection of crops and the purchase of seeds will be properly guided by various cooperative instructors, and a seed committee will be organized to be responsible for handling them. The results of winter cultivation will be reported by the supervisory committees of each county, according to the cultivated area, location, crop type, and quantity filled in the loan contract, and reported to the Cooperation Bureau for record. The responsibility for agricultural technical guidance and loan collection will be handled by the Cooperation Affairs Bureau, assisted by the Agricultural Improvement Office and the county governments.

The Fujian Provincial Government recently implemented grain management to ensure food self-sufficiency and prevent unscrupulous merchants from smuggling, hoarding, and speculating. According to the method, each county uniformly organizes a grain management committee. Before the early and late rice harvest each year, the local baojia chiefs will conduct a comprehensive survey of the number of mu of rice planted by the owners and farmers in the bao, and estimate their harvest, filling out a form and reporting it to the district office, which will report it to the county grain management committee for verification. The owner's family should report the actual harvest quantity to the local baojia chief within one week after the harvest, filling out a form and reporting it to the district office, which will forward it to the county grain management committee. The owner's family should also report the quantity of remaining rice in addition to the necessary consumption for the whole family to the baojia chief in charge, who will forward it to the district office, which will report it to the county grain management committee for record. If they want to sell it, they should report to the grain management committee, which will coordinate the sale according to the market price and must not sell it themselves. If the number of rice harvested by the owner's family is underreported or falsely reported, and they intend to hoard and speculate, hindering people's food supply, once discovered or reported, in addition to confiscating the underreported or falsely reported portion, they will be given appropriate punishment. If the baojia chief assists in concealing it, or takes the opportunity to engage in favoritism and fraud, they will also be punished according to law. The grain management committees of each county may also conduct surveys of the local grain situation and formulate wholesale and retail prices of rice and other grains on a weekly basis, submit them to the meeting for evaluation, and then present them to the local主管 government for announcement.

Shanghai Municipal Council Approves Increase in Tuition Fees for Western and Chinese Children's Schools; Western Schools to Increase by 25% Next Month; Chinese Schools to Increase by 15% Next Spring 41

The Education Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council, in view of the large increase in expenses required for the various schools established by the Council, held two meetings on the 15th and 29th of last month to consider the issue of increasing tuition fees. It was found that the educational expenses required this year were expected to exceed the amount stated in the budget by 340,000 national currency. If the current situation continues unchanged, the financial situation next year will be even more unfavorable. The summary of income and expenditure of the various Council-run schools is listed below:

The expenditure of each Chinese children's school next year will increase by 38.5% compared with last year, and the income will increase by 11.6%. The increase in expenditure of Western children's schools is greater, so the increase in tuition fees should also be greater. As for the method of increasing fees, it is appropriate to collect a certain percentage of surcharges. After detailed discussion by the Education Committee, it was resolved to request the Board of Directors to approve an increase in tuition fees for all Western children's schools by 25% from November 1st of this year, and for all Chinese children's schools by 15% from the spring of next year. The total surcharge can collect one million yuan per year. The above recommendations have been approved by the Shanghai Municipal Council at its regular meeting on the 4th of this month.

Finance Exporters Dumping Foreign Exchange in the Market, Immediately Recovers After Tightening 49

Yesterday's foreign exchange market situation: listed exchange rates did not fluctuate. The under-the-table market for British and American currencies stabilized slightly as various rumors in the market gradually dissipated. However, trading started soft in the morning due to weak selling interest from foreign banks. Subsequently, the Bank of England (on behalf of a certain group) absorbed heavily, and the Yokohama Specie Bank also followed suit. Although foreign telegrams from Hong Kong and exporters were mutually supplying and dumping, positions were still difficult to allocate, causing the British pound to continue to tighten to 4 shillings and 3.75 pence, and the US dollar to also soften to 7.375 yuan. Later, as telegrams from Hong Kong and exporters continued to show strong selling interest, and the British merchant Sassoon also came to dump, the Bank of America (arbitrage on rupees) also had an oversupply, so the situation gradually recovered. The evening close for the British pound was still 4 shillings and a half, and the US dollar was 7.5625 yuan. The trend for this month's futures was similar to the spot market, and trading was brisk throughout the day.

At the beginning of the morning, the London cable indicated that near-term futures were down by 3.75 pence, and far-term futures were down by 4.375 pence. The New York silver price fell by 0.125. Small Denomination Notes Difficult to Exchange 51

Since the Central Bank of China issued small denomination notes in Shanghai, it has been generally believed that it can alleviate the pain of small transactions. Since the start of issuance on the 29th of last month, it has been more than a week, but the small denomination notes circulating in the market are still extremely rare. Peddlers and various shops still use substitute vouchers and tram tickets for small change, and because the acceptance of these types of vouchers is frequent, they are tattered and often cause disputes. The small ones not only lose convenience, but also increase the burden on life, and the large ones are related to the entire national monetary system. This is because the Central Bank does not set up exchange offices, so most shops and residents have nowhere to exchange them, and unified industry exchange makes them a rare commodity. One yuan notes can only be exchanged for 9 jiao, and recently some yuan can be exchanged for 9 jiao and 5 fen. It is said that the amount is too small and cannot meet the needs of the entire Shanghai, like a cart of firewood for a cup of water. Therefore, for the benefit of the majority, the Central Bank should increase the amount of issuance and entrust various banks and money shops to exchange them, so as to avoid congestion and benefit the people. The Truth About the Stalled Negotiations on the Western Shanghai Issue: The Issue of Police Power Seems Easier to Resolve, The Pseudo-Regime Is Determined to Interfere With the Collection of Taxes 65

Yesterday afternoon, a certain official of the concession told reporters that the intrusion of pseudo-police into the road construction area outside the boundary, the unauthorized deployment of outposts and patrols, and the directing of traffic can no longer be regarded as temporary matters. The focus of negotiations between the Municipal Council and the pseudo-municipal government is on re-allocating the area and powers of the road construction area in the Western District outside the boundary. At this time, due to the issues of taxes and police power, there were significant differences in opinion between the two parties, and the negotiations could not continue. Since the establishment of the Shanghai Refugee Relief Association, in addition to raising funds to assist various charitable organizations in handling accommodation and relief, it also pays attention to post-disaster matters such as evacuation, relocation, employment placement, and production work. According to Mr. Yuan Ludeng, Secretary-General of the Association, the number of refugees registered for employment by the Employment Placement Group from February to the end of September in various accommodation centers is as follows: 319 female workers in yarn factories, 48 coppersmiths, 37 chefs, 55 printing workers, 43 teachers, 31 clerks, 23 female workers in sock factories, 53 machinists, 20 painters, 7 embroiderers, 31 workers in silk factories, 114 workers in tobacco factories, 46 weavers, 71 workers in rubber galoshes factories, 3 electrical engineers, 14 silk weavers, 20 carpenters, 29 tailors, 21 plasterers, and other skilled and unskilled workers, totaling 2,257 people. 468 people have been directly placed by the group, including 163 female workers in yarn factories, 30 female workers in porcelain factories, and others who have taken on other jobs. The number of refugees who have been indirectly employed with the assistance of various accommodation centers is not included. The association also provides subsidies to refugees during their apprenticeship, to show compassion and reduce the burden on employers. It is still hoped that all sectors will give priority to employing refugees when they need labor, turning division of profits into production, and transforming passive charity into active relief. Replacing relief with work and benefiting the people is certainly not a small matter. Please contact Mr. Li Wenjie, Director of the Employment Placement Group, and Mr. Li Baiqiang, Deputy Director, at 12669 at any time for consultation.

Japanese Force Relocation of Muslim Cemetery; Muslim Community Holds Emergency Meeting; Strenuously Argue for Route Change to Preserve Original State; Matter Concerns Religious Property, Attracting Citywide Muslim Attention 76

The Zhenru Muslim Cemetery is being forcibly moved because the Japanese are planning to build a railway there. The Fuyou Road Mosque has convened a citywide meeting of representatives from various Muslim organizations. The result was a decision by the Muslims to work together in the coming days to negotiate with the Japanese based on reason, demanding a change of route in order to preserve the original state of the cemetery. A reporter from Daguan News Agency has investigated and reported the situation as follows:

Muslim Representatives' Emergency Meeting

The Zhenru Muslim Cemetery and the Niuye Guild land originally belonged to the Fuyou Road Mosque and comprised more than twenty mu, with approximately eight hundred graves. After the cemetery keeper reported to the mosque that the Japanese were planning to seize the cemetery land to build a railway, forcing the relocation of graves, the mosque posted notices to all families of the deceased, soliciting opinions for discussion at the meeting. At the same time, they printed leaflets explaining the truth of the matter and distributed them to Muslims throughout the city. Upon hearing the news, Muslim organizations throughout the city were extremely indignant and convened an emergency meeting of Muslim representatives the previous evening. Over forty representatives from mosques and missions in Fuyou Road, Zhejiang Road, Xiaoshadu Road, Pudong, and Hudong attended. A representative from the Fuyou Road Mosque reported on the Japanese seizure of the cemetery land. Representatives expressed their opinions separately, their emotions were agitated, and their attitudes were indignant. It was decided that Muslims would work together to negotiate with the Japanese based on reason, demanding a change of route to preserve the original state of the cemetery. They then discussed the opinions of the families of the deceased and adjourned the meeting around 9 p.m.

Matter Concerns Religious Property, Struggle Based on Reason

Yesterday, a spokesperson for the Muslim community told the Daguan News Agency that Islam originated in Mecca, Egypt (referred to as "Tianfang" by Muslims). The prophet is Muhammad. Countries around the world, such as Turkey, Egypt, the Balkans, India, Abyssinia, Australia, England, America, France, Germany, Italy, Russia, and Japan, all have Muslim populations. Islam in China dates back to the Tang Dynasty. There are over 30 million Muslims throughout the country, with the largest populations in the northwest in Xinjiang, Gansu, and Ningxia, followed by various provinces, cities, and counties. The Japanese seizure of the Muslim cemetery is not just a matter for the Fuyou Road Mosque; it is a matter for all Muslims in the city and the country, and even for Muslims in countries around the world. Given the significance, the Fuyou Road Mosque authorities do not dare to act alone and rashly adopt any measures to negotiate with the Japanese. News will be communicated to Muslims throughout the city at any time to determine how to respond. They will argue reasonably. A Cantonese man, He Muxi, 61 years old, living at No. 4 Dexing Lane, North Jiangxi Road, recently purchased several large bundles of firewood from a certain place. Last night, He used a knife to split the bamboo hoops on the firewood, but in the center of the firewood was a bomb. After He vigorously chopped the wood, the bomb was detonated by the impact. He's left and right hands were injured and he was transported to Renji Hospital by ambulance. It is said that his right hand has been blown off.

Free Transport of Rice to Shanghai Resolved; Rice Prices Plummet; Approximately 10,000 Bags Arrive in Shanghai Daily; Food Supply No Longer Feared to be Scarce 77

New rice from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui has successively entered the market, and due to favorable weather, there has been a bumper harvest. The issue of free transport of rice to Shanghai has also been resolved. As a result, various rice industry groups are making every effort to dredge sources of supply, purchasing from various producing areas, transporting rice to Shanghai for market adjustment. In recent days, the volume of rice transported by river, train and ship from Kunshan, Changzhou, Jiaxing, Wuhu, Songjiang and other places has been from 8,000 to 15,000 bags per day. As a result, Shanghai's stock of rice has gradually increased, market prices have fallen by three to four yuan, and the trend is expected to continue. Therefore, there is no concern of lack of food. Furthermore, although the arrival of rice in Shanghai has been surging, it is all Jiangbei Xian rice, therefore, although the price of Xian rice has continued to fall, the price of Bai Geng rice has remained stable. Yesterday, a large number of Songjiang Bai Geng rice, no less than 8,000 bags, was transported by river. As a result, the opening price of this Bai Geng rice in the rice market yesterday fell by five yuan per shi. The price per shi, which was originally 37 yuan, has fallen to 32 yuan yesterday. Jiangbei Xian rice also continued to fall by one yuan per shi due to the continued arrival of goods, with the highest price being 31 yuan. However, due to the scarcity of Changshu Bai Geng rice, the price per shi still costs 42 yuan. As for Nanjing brown rice, the price per shi is only 18 yuan. If transportation is not obstructed in the future, prices should not be expected to rise.

Lou Buqing, son of the deceased former head of the Shanghai Songhu Police Department's Investigation Team, section chief of the second district of the Jiangsu Water Police, and native of Hangzhou, Zhejiang (34 years old this year, currently residing at No. 4, Yi Li, Fahuaxi Town, Columbia Road, Shanghai, formerly worked in the baggage room of the Suzhou Railway Station on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, and left his job when the Suzhou station was evacuated after the 83 war). Two brothers

the time of the property division,

Prodigal Son Murders Elderly Father; Demanding Money Unsuccessfully, Suddenly Arouses Murderous Intent; Administers Electric Current and Slashes with a Knife; Elderly Father Dies Tragically, Unfilial Son Arrested 85

Zhou Yongjie, a native of Ningbo, 50 years old, lives at No. A228 Haig Road, Western Shanghai. In his early years, he ran a business and was quite diligent, so he had some savings. Zhou has a son, around 20 years old, who usually hangs out with hooligans, practices inferior habits, and repeatedly demands money from his father to squander outside. Recently, he repeatedly demanded money from his father, but Zhou did not give him any. His son therefore harbored resentment in his heart. Around 10 o'clock last night, Zhou's son suddenly had an evil idea and went to Zhou Yongjie's bedroom, seeing his father sleeping sweetly in bed. Zhou's son connected an electric wire to the current, one end attached to Zhou Yongjie's body. After Zhou was electrocuted, he fainted. Tax on Cotton Scraps and Cotton Waste; Five Gold Units Taxed per Hundred Catties 88

The Customs announced the resolution of the August tariff issue, number 469, commodity name: cotton scraps and cotton waste, question: should it be classified as cotton or waste cotton? Resolution: Cotton scraps and cotton waste are the materials removed during the combing and brushing of cotton and can be used for spinning. They should be classified into item 71 of the import tariff, cotton, taxed at five gold units per hundred kilograms.

Xujiahui Observatory, yesterday at 4:30 p.m. Meteorological forecast: The weather around Shandong is variable, the wind is nondirectional, due to the low pressure that has passed through Korea and is advancing to the southeast-east. It is clear here, with southwest to northwest winds. There are northwest to northeast winds in the East China Sea. The center of the hurricane advanced to within 120 miles of 14 degrees north latitude and 136 degrees east longitude before 6 a.m., wind direction northwest-west, wind force unknown. Also, within 24 hours before 3 p.m. yesterday, the temperature in this city was high at 84.6 and low at 55.4. On the same day last year, the highest was 87.4 and the lowest was 66.2.

Reported News of Applicants for Radio Operator Examinations: Mr. Gong Allegedly Used the Name of the Aviation Administration to Organize a Fake Examination; The School Providing the Exam Site Should Also Be Held Responsible 90

To the Esteemed Editor:

We are a group of graduates from the Wireless Radio Specialization Department of the First China Vocational Supplementary School. Around the time of our graduation, a classmate, Mr. So-and-so, informed us that the Inland Aviation Administration and the Transportation Department (Southwest Highway) radio stations were recruiting over eighty radio operators in Shanghai. The lowest monthly salary was eighty yuan (for a third-class operator). After being hired, travel expenses to the interior would be subsidized by the organization. The first examination was to be held at the ×× Wireless Radio Specialized School. What a wonderful opportunity! We were all filled with joy, hoping that after passing the exam, we could realize our dream—to serve our motherland!

This was on July 18th. We went to the ×× School to register and learned that the examination would be held at 6:00 PM on the 19th. At that time, according to the regulations, we each paid a registration fee of two yuan, and submitted two photos and resumes. With the receipt in hand, we waited for the 19th. That day was when a typhoon hit Shanghai, and it rained heavily. Braving the wind and rain, we rushed to the ×× Radio School for the examination. Upon arrival, we saw a notice posted stating that the examiner, a radio operator from the ×× Shipping Company, surnamed Gong, named ××, had been delayed due to the typhoon preventing the ship from docking, so the examination would be postponed. We then returned home. For three consecutive days, it was all for naught. We were very surprised. How could a state institution be so unreliable with its examination schedule? However, we believed that the ×× Radio School had a considerable history and reputation in Shanghai, so it would certainly not engage in falsehoods to deceive us young people.

The examination was held at 6:00 PM on the 22nd. One chief examiner and three or four proctors were present, with over thirty applicants. After four hours, the examination ended. At this time, our heavy hearts gradually lightened, and we only hoped for the results to be announced. Several days later, we learned that some of us (the writers of this letter) had been accepted. How delighted we were! Our hopes were about to be realized! We were also told that we would have to depart within two months. Therefore, we all prepared our luggage, waiting to embrace our motherland and serve the country two months later. At that time, we felt indescribable joy and relief!

Now, two months have passed since the examination date. Ah! Truly, "the heavens have unpredictable winds, and humans have sudden misfortunes." A few days ago, we suddenly received a mimeographed letter from the ×× Radio School sent to each applicant. After reading the letter, it was like a bolt from the blue, shocking everyone. The letter stated: "The examiner, Gong ××, has not yet provided a departure date, and is now even demanding a security deposit of five yuan per person... This method seems deceitful, so we have decided to immediately refund the registration fees previously collected..." We still cannot figure out how such a reputable radio school could do such a senseless thing. Mr. Gong used the school as an examination site, so prior arrangements must have been made, and the school must have trusted Mr. Gong. We trusted the ×× Radio School. Our registration fees were paid at the school's accounting office, and we took the examination at the school, so the ×× Radio School must bear responsibility. Unexpectedly, this is the result, which has surprised us all... Alas! Because of this so-called opportunity, we waited wholeheartedly for two months. Knowing that we had been accepted and would be sent to work in the interior, we did not apply for the openly advertised radio operator positions at schools such as the St. Louis Radio School recently. Who knew that now the ×× Radio School would inform the applicants that this matter was a fraud. Then, won't we have to look for another opportunity? But when will we have the chance? It has been over two months since we graduated from school. If things continue like this, won't the skills we have learned gradually decline and become rusty? The youth's time is the most precious time in life. Waiting like this on a deserted island is a significant loss for us! (Responsibility for the text rests with the author)

The Sky After the Rain 91

— Bao

Chapter Sixteen: Planning to Promote Medical Education and Build Schools; Thinking About Expanding Village Governance and Providing Care for Children

There is another bad custom: using celebrations and condolences as a way to make money and seek profit. This is less common in the countryside, but more prevalent in cities. For example, when an old lady turns a certain age, her birthday must indeed be celebrated, and the post-birthday feast cannot be forgone. When a stepmother turns a certain age, her birthday must indeed be celebrated, but the biological mother's celebration must be even more lively. In addition, birthdays of paternal aunts, maternal aunts, mothers-in-law, and foster mothers are all opportunities to gather materials for birthday celebrations. There are even cases where a birthday is celebrated in the first half of the year, and another one is celebrated in the second half. If the old lady has already passed away, then a posthumous birthday can be celebrated if a regular one cannot. Later, the death anniversaries of parents and grandparents are treated the same as regular birthdays, with invitations sent out widely and gifts collected extensively. In reality, when a person is dead, what birthday is there? If it stems from sincere remembrance, family rituals and memorial services are acceptable, but why the need for such grand displays? This shows that the intention is not really about the celebration. Later, Shanghai's pleasure-seekers even sought revenge and retaliation because of not sending gifts when sending invitations, resulting in violent altercations. The matter of gift-giving can be said to have reached its extreme. Therefore, there was a backlash later, with society generally refraining from giving gifts for celebrations and condolences. If close relatives and friends occasionally offer a gift, that is an exception. The gifts given are either souvenirs or necessities. Items like banners and silver shields are completely useless waste, and of course, they have disappeared. Even the market no longer sells such items. Therefore, there were very few people giving gifts at Lin Jiancheng and Jin Danyun's wedding this time. However, one cannot say there were absolutely none. Close friends and confidants also gave them gifts, but they could give them at any time, without having to crowd around at this particular moment. Just like among her sisters, Zhu Airen might not give her anything, but the He sisters would definitely give something. It is unknown what the Wu Junsou sisters would do, but they would probably give some souvenirs. It is guessed that Mrs. Su Liya's gift would be the biggest. At eight o'clock on Friday morning, Zhu Village Chief called his granddaughter. He said, "Yesterday, the village council meeting was held, and the matter of the He sisters' silk weaving factory site has been approved. However, what kind of building will be built in the future? What kind of equipment will be used? The layout will still have to be reviewed once. You inform them both!" Airen obediently agreed, and also told him, "I won't be coming to Freedom Village next week because everyone is going to Shanghai to attend Jin Danyun's wedding. Also, the He sisters received a telegram from their grandfather saying that a paternal elder is coming to Shanghai from the north, and they will also go to visit him to discuss the silk factory. Because that paternal elder is currently a shareholder and used to run a silk weaving factory, he is an expert who should be consulted." (188)

Gas Lamps (Mechanical Poetic Talk) 92

— Ru Hui

Before electric lights, Shanghai also had "gas lamps."

Wang Tao's "Ying Ruan Magazine" (1875), Volume Six, states:

Westerners have erected lamps in the streets, spaced closely or sparsely according to distance. The lamps are all made of hexagonal glass, shining like stars from afar. Later, they were replaced with gas, which is even brighter. This is because the gas from coal mines is gathered and ignited, so the light is far-reaching and dazzling... It can be seen that "gas lamps" appeared in Shanghai during the Tongzhi reign of the Qing dynasty, and were regarded as "miracles." Therefore, people at the time created the "Ten Views of Northern Shanghai," and this was one of them, titled "Night Market Lamps," and they praised it with the following verse:

Thousands of electric lights connect iron pipes,

Most suitable for dance halls and singing banquets.

No need to envy the purple light offerings of old,

A city that never sleeps all night long.

At that time, Shanghai had only a few "gas lamps," but it became a "city that never sleeps." However, this is not an "exaggeration." Ciqi Zhiting's "Four Poems on Yangjing" described the mystery of "gas lamps" even more vividly. The poem reads:

Living fire burns thousands of flowers,

Bright stars illuminate ten thousand homes.

Pavilions are never dark in spring nights,

The scenery is vast and boundless.

Trying to outshine the silver toad [moon],

Truly opening iron tree blossoms.

Climbing high and looking far,

Seemingly scattering red city clouds.

The topic is called "Ground Fire," which was a very common name at the time. The old owner of Twenty-Three Rooms also filled in "Looking South of the River" to praise it, calling it:

Shanghai is good, ground fire is the brightest.

The bronze dragon counts the hours, boasting a sleepless night,

Iron trees bloom, illuminating the deep night,

Even clearer than the moon.

This is written in a more tranquil way. However, most writers only regarded it as the moon. Su Kanghou's poem: "No need to carry candles in this scenic spot, round pearls replace the moon and are even brighter. No need to waste money to buy, heaven opens a city that never sleeps at sea." is of this kind. "Shanghai Northern Bamboo Branch" also praised "ground fire":

Thousands of lamps stand west to east,

Fire comes naturally, seizing the work of nature.

No need to burn tallow to boast of extending the day,

Night walks are always in the moonlight.

The end note says: "Lamps are placed on poles to illuminate the road. The fire comes from underground passages, the light is extremely bright and never goes out all night." Therefore, at the time, "gas lamps" were also called "self-lighting fire." As for "ground fire all night," "Shenpu Bamboo Branch Words" also mentioned it, saying that "ground fire passes through everywhere." The poem directly praising it reads:

Most ingenious is the smokeless ground fire,

Bright light, faces slightly flushed.

Up and down the building, all are illuminated,

Who can discern the mechanisms in the dark?

The last two lines are very good. The strangest is the author of "Shanghai City Miscellaneous Poems," who cursed "gas lamps" as "ghost fire," calling "ghost fire clustering like stars, Zhang Hai Market." This person was probably a very conservative type. But most authors only had praise. Until "electric lights" were established, the enthusiasm for praising "ground fire" turned to "electric lights." However, in the early days of "electric lights," which was also the transitional period from "gas lamps" to "electric lights," there were also those who praised both sides. This is evidenced by the "Shanghai Bamboo Branch Words" of the owner of the Southern Border Double Red Bean Pavilion:

Shanghai is clearly a city that never sleeps,

Electric lights and gas lamps compete in beauty.

Making people unable to distinguish the round moon,

Let alone say tonight is the Lantern Festival.
