Entertainment World

Two Stages Compete to Hire Xun Huisheng; There Are Still Problems with His Coming to Shanghai 93

— Only Me

Xun Huisheng, one of the Four Great Dan performers, has not come south to perform since his appearance at the Tianchan Stage in the twenty-second year, which is already six years ago. (Three years ago, Huisheng once came to Shanghai to attend Zhang Xiaolin's sixtieth birthday celebration.) Precisely because of this, the Golden Theater and the Renewal Stage both want to invite Mr. Xun to Shanghai. After the two theaters sent people to contact Huisheng separately, the news of Xun Huisheng's coming to Shanghai to perform spread to almost every Peking Opera enthusiast's ears.

After many twists and turns, as a result of the two theaters' unrelenting efforts, the truth tells us this: Xun Huisheng will come south in mid-September of the lunar calendar, and the heads of the two theaters will resolve this difficult problem with emotions. ——Xun Huisheng will first perform at the Renewal Stage for half a month (taking over from Wu Suqiu, Zhao Jinrong, and others), and after that, he will go to the Golden Theater for one month (taking over from Wang Yurong). Unexpectedly, after the Renewal Stage's talent scout Chang returned to Shanghai to report back, Xun Huisheng suddenly sent a telegram to a certain influential person connected to Renewal, saying that he did not acknowledge having reached an agreement with the Renewal talent scout to come to Shanghai on time to take over from Wu Suqiu and others. Therefore, the matter of Huisheng's coming to Shanghai has changed again in unseen ways.

It is said that Huisheng and Renewal have not reached an agreement because of business matters. Xun Huisheng is treating Renewal with an attitude of recognizing money but not people, wanting to use a huge performance fee to make the Renewal authorities give up on him. His intention is that after Renewal gives up, he can resolutely come to Shanghai to perform at the Golden Theater. In fact, the Golden Theater had indeed formally invited Huisheng a long time ago.

The Renewal Stage's matter with Huisheng now hinges entirely on a difference in numbers. Renewal's General Manager Mr. Dong Zhaobin's intention is to express discouragement because of Huisheng's deliberate obstruction. However, after hearing "a casual remark" from a certain influential person, if the influential person's intention is that there is no need to invite him again, the Renewal authorities will decisively give up on Xun Huisheng and bring Tan Fuying and Tan Xiaopei, father and son, to Shanghai to perform ahead of schedule. As for the Golden Theater, because they had smooth negotiations with Huisheng before, they expressed great confidence in Huisheng's coming to Shanghai.

The affairs of opera troupes are often infinitely variable. It is possible that Xun Huisheng can still meet the people of Shanghai according to the original plan. However, besides this problem, there is another problem, which is that Wang Yurong's supporting actors, the young male lead Jin Zhongren, the clown Zhu Binxian, and the painted face Jiang Shaoqiu, are all members of Xun Huisheng's troupe. If Wang Yurong performs at the Golden Theater before Huisheng, Jin Zhongren and others will have to come with Yurong. There is no problem with this on the Golden Theater's side, but on the Renewal side, it is an unexpected complication because in reality, it is absolutely not allowed for Jin Zhongren and others to perform in both theaters.

It is said that Xun Huisheng's staff members and supporting cast all want to come south. Huisheng himself is not unwilling to come to Shanghai. However, all leading actors have a certain arrogance, which is that if someone invites him, he must put on a full display of airs. I am also a member who loves and protects Huisheng. I hope Boss Xun will not be too much like that. Because this decision is undoubtedly giving Huisheng a great opportunity. One must know that opportunities are not always available. If this opportunity is missed, I am afraid there will not be such a good opportunity again.

After the Outbreak of the European War: The Trend of Hollywood 94

— New Film

After a considerable period of brewing, the European war has finally transitioned from a propaganda war to a formal war. Although Hollywood, the world's only film city, is separated by vast oceans, it has been significantly affected by the European war. In particular, the following points are especially prominent:

Changing Film Production Policies Europe is the largest overseas market for American films, especially Britain, which is an excellent market for Hollywood productions. Therefore, this European war has severely hit the overseas market for Hollywood films, especially since Britain is also one of the main warring countries. As a result, Hollywood film companies immediately changed their policies regarding film production, and all films centered on European film audiences were stopped from being filmed.

Movie Stars Return Home to Serve When we recall the previous European war, many foreign movie stars in Hollywood returned home to serve, some even fighting on the battlefield. So this time, after the outbreak of the European war, it is certainly no exception that foreign movie stars will be conscripted back home. For example, Charles Boyer has returned to France to serve, and people like Colman have also returned to England. If the war continues, there will certainly be many more foreign film workers who will return to their countries to take on various wartime tasks and serve their country!

Promoting the South American Market In recent years, the Spanish war and the Sino-Japanese conflict have reduced Hollywood's overseas film market. The outbreak of this European war has had an even more serious impact on Hollywood. In this situation, Hollywood film companies have shifted their attention to South American countries, making every effort to promote the market in South America and Central America. Therefore, we have recently seen films depicting South American scenery being shown continuously, which is also a shift in Hollywood's direction in the midst of the European war!

New Film Introduction

Splendid Rivers and Mountains 95

— Enterprise

"Juarez"

"Splendid Rivers and Mountains" narrates the story of Mexican President Juarez in the mid-19th century, resisting the French army that invaded Mexico. Although most of the cities were captured, and although the puppet Maximilian was crowned under the instigation of Napoleon III, Juarez remained calm and firm. He rejected Maximilian's moderation and extinguished the rebellion of Vice President Urandi with the fire of justice. Finally, with the support of the military and the people, Juarez recovered Mexico's splendid rivers and mountains.

From this story, it gives us the following lessons: (1) Juarez's indomitable spirit of resistance finally led to the final victory; while the French army, which traveled long distances and hoped to fulfill its ambitions of aggression, was inevitably doomed to failure. (2) Maximilian's puppet appearance was indeed deceived by General Baron. When he discovered that Baron wanted him to sign a document authorizing the confiscation of people's property and the execution of those who privately stored military supplies, he still hoped to "cooperate" with Juarez. He did not completely see that in the autumn of national survival, there is only absolute "yes" and "no," and there is no middle ground. (3) Vice President Urandi's conspiracy and rebellion also finally collapsed before justice.

The role of Juarez is played by Paul Muni. With his refined acting skills, he plays the great man in history. His bright and energetic eyes and firm and calm demeanor are truly awe-inspiring! The role of Maximilian is played by Brian Aherne. From his puppet appearance, being deceived, compromising, to failing, he can portray the conflict of psychological contradictions in every process, which is completely different from the unrefined hero Fleury in "New Gold Mountain." Bette Davis, as Maximilian's wife Carlota, demonstrates her superb acting skills in comforting her husband and going mad after seeing Napoleon. (To be continued)

Outside the Pear Garden 96

— Xu

Shanghai Should Create a Theater for Joint Performances of Qin, Pi, and Huang Operas

Recently, Song Dezhu's "Jinshan Temple" has been staged at the Sun Theater. This play combines civil, military, Kunqu, and miscellaneous styles in a furnace, deeply catering to Shanghai customers' tastes. The skillful and steady fighting at the end, combined with the tight and rigorous stage presence, makes the whole play impeccable, with no one missing a beat or leaving the stage. This is truly a rare occurrence in fighting plays. What is wonderful is that, in addition to the drummer and cymbal player who are slightly older, the others, such as those playing the erhu, sanxian, moon guitar, and small drums, are all children around ten years old. This situation is probably only seen by Shanghai residents. It is not well known that the Beijing Opera School originally had a music theory department, with the renowned Cao Xinquan responsible for guidance. Therefore, many students of the school are able to master the stage thoroughly. Those who came with Xing Dezhu this time are probably alumni who graduated from the same department. In recent years, many new famous musicians have emerged, but many can only play the erhu and are not skilled in the flute and sona. Compared to the students of opera school, they are truly ashamed.

After watching this play, I have a lot of feelings. If we only talk about the first half of "Jinshan Temple," Dezhu may not be better than Han Shichang of the Northern Kunqu Opera Troupe. However, if we compare the current situations of Han and Song, it is simply one in the underground and one in the sky. In recent years, Peking Opera has developed abnormally, and Kunqu and Qin Opera have almost been submerged into obscurity. A few years ago, Shichang, in order to maintain the livelihood of his colleagues, once again acted as Feng Fu, performing in various ports in Pingjin. However, because the audience was sparse and the ticket prices were low, the daily ticket income was not enough to cover the cost of food and lodging for the entire troupe. Because Shichang still had income from teaching opera at a certain mansion, he declared that he was completely voluntary, and even his transportation expenses were not covered. However, he still had to pay the salary of one yuan to the employee who dressed his hair every day. ——(114)
